    51	
    52	
    53	class NotificationError(RuntimeError):
    54	    pass
    55	
    56	
    57	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    58	# Transient-network resilience (shared by every outbound Slack POST)
    59	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    60	# A transient DNS/network blip shouldn't lose a Slack post. We make 4 attempts
    61	# total, sleeping 5s/15s/30s BEFORE attempts 2/3/4, and retry ONLY on transient
    62	# transport errors (the requests/urllib network-error families). A successful
    63	# HTTP exchange that carries a bad status is NOT retried here — callers keep
    64	# their own success/non-200 handling, so failure behavior is unchanged once the
    65	# transport itself succeeds. See the Coverage Manager reporting/slack.py
    66	# reference impl (urlopen_with_retry).
    67	_RETRY_BACKOFF = (5, 15, 30)  # seconds to wait BEFORE retry attempts 2..N
    68	
    69	
    70	def _retry_sleep(seconds: float) -> None:
    71	    # Skip the wall-clock wait under pytest (which sets PYTEST_CURRENT_TEST) so
    72	    # the network-error tests don't sleep through the full backoff.
    73	    import os
    74	    import time
    75	    if not os.environ.get("PYTEST_CURRENT_TEST"):
    76	        time.sleep(seconds)
    77	
    78	
    79	def post_with_retry(*args, attempts: int = 4, label: str = "slack post", **kwargs):
    80	    """``requests.post`` with backoff retry on transient transport errors.
    81	
    82	    Re-raises the last ``requests.exceptions.RequestException`` if every attempt
    83	    fails, so existing callers keep their fallback/raise behavior on a genuine
    84	    outage — this only rides through momentary blips. Calls ``requests.post`` by
    85	    name so test monkeypatches still intercept it. Does NOT inspect the response
    86	    status; a successful-but-bad-status response is returned to the caller as-is.
    87	    """
    88	    last = None
    89	    for i in range(attempts):
    90	        try:
    91	            return requests.post(*args, **kwargs)
    92	        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as exc:
    93	            last = exc
    94	            if i < attempts - 1:
    95	                delay = _RETRY_BACKOFF[min(i, len(_RETRY_BACKOFF) - 1)]
    96	                logger.warning("%s attempt %d/%d failed (%s); retrying in %ds",
    97	                               label, i + 1, attempts, exc, delay)
    98	                _retry_sleep(delay)
    99	    raise last
   100	
   101	
   102	def urlopen_with_retry(req, *, timeout: int = 10, attempts: int = 4,
   103	                       label: str = "slack post"):
   104	    """``urllib.request.urlopen`` with backoff retry on transient transport errors.
   105	
   106	    Re-raises the last ``urllib.error.URLError`` if every attempt fails, so
   107	    existing callers keep their swallow/return behavior on a genuine outage.
   108	    Calls ``urllib.request.urlopen`` by name so monkeypatches still intercept it.
   109	    """
   110	    import urllib.request
   111	    import urllib.error
   112	    last = None
   113	    for i in range(attempts):
   114	        try:
   115	            return urllib.request.urlopen(req, timeout=timeout)
   116	        except urllib.error.URLError as exc:
   117	            last = exc
   118	            if i < attempts - 1:
   119	                delay = _RETRY_BACKOFF[min(i, len(_RETRY_BACKOFF) - 1)]
   120	                logger.warning("%s attempt %d/%d failed (%s); retrying in %ds",
   121	                               label, i + 1, attempts, exc, delay)
   122	                _retry_sleep(delay)
   123	    raise last
   124	
   125	
   126	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   127	# Shared formatting helpers
   128	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   129	
   130	
   131	def _timing_short(hour: str | None) -> str:
   132	    if not hour:
   133	        return "TBD"
   134	    h = hour.lower()
   135	    if h == "bmo":
   136	        return "BMO"
   137	    if h == "amc":
   138	        return "AMC"
   139	    if h == "dmh":
   140	        return "DMH"
   141	    return hour.upper()
   142	
   143	
   144	def _fmt_date_safe(iso: str) -> str:
   145	    # Avoid %-d / %#d platform quirks by formatting the day manually.
   146	    d = date.fromisoformat(iso)
   147	    return f"{d.strftime('%a %b')} {d.day}"
   148	
   149	
   150	def _fmt_estimate_eps(eps: float | None) -> str:
   151	    if eps is None:
   152	        return "–"
   153	    return f"${eps:.2f}"
   154	
   155	
   156	def _fmt_estimate_rev(rev: float | None) -> str:
   157	    if rev is None:
   158	        return "–"
   159	    if rev >= 1e9:
   160	        return f"${rev / 1e9:.2f}B"
   161	    if rev >= 1e6:
   162	        return f"${rev / 1e6:.1f}M"
   163	    return f"${rev:,.0f}"
   164

I found one area worth deeper validation: the preview’s own `SLACK_MAX_BLOCKS` is 48 while Slack’s real message limit is 50, but the truncation can still leave many covered reporters unposted while the dedupe loop marks every assembled row. I’m checking whether that is a genuine live data-loss path or just a low-severity presentation limit.

   255	def init_db(db_path: Path = DB_PATH) -> sqlite3.Connection:
   256	    """
   257	    Initialize the SQLite database with non-destructive migrations.
   258	
   259	    - Creates the schema from scratch if the database is new.
   260	    - Applies incremental migrations for existing databases.
   261	    - Never drops tables or deletes data.
   262	    """
   263	    conn = sqlite3.connect(str(db_path))
   264	
   265	    # Ensure schema_version table exists
   266	    conn.execute("""
   267	        CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS schema_version (
   268	            version INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,
   269	            applied_at TEXT NOT NULL
   270	        )
   271	    """)
   272	    conn.commit()
   273	
   274	    current_version = _get_schema_version(conn)
   275	
   276	    if not _table_exists(conn, "events"):
   277	        # Fresh database — create the full schema
   278	        conn.execute("""
   279	            CREATE TABLE events (
   280	                id              INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
   281	                ticker          TEXT    NOT NULL,
   282	                quarter         TEXT,
   283	                event_date      TEXT    NOT NULL,
   284	                event_hour      TEXT,
   285	                gcal_id         TEXT,
   286	                eps_estimate    REAL,
   287	                eps_actual      REAL,
   288	                rev_estimate    REAL,
   289	                rev_actual      REAL,
   290	                reported        INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
   291	                tier            INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 3,
   292	                source_fingerprint TEXT,
   293	                company_name    TEXT,
   294	                ir_url          TEXT,
   295	                call_url        TEXT,
   296	                ticktick_task_id TEXT,
   297	                unseen_run_count INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
   298	                date_locked     INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
   299	                last_xcheck_yf_dates TEXT,
   300	                date_confirmed  INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
   301	                announcement_url TEXT,
   302	                slack_thread_ts TEXT,
   303	                slack_question_kind TEXT,
   304	                slack_last_reply_ts TEXT,
   305	                question_state  TEXT,
   306	                question_snooze_until TEXT,
   307	                question_first_seen TEXT,
   308	                slack_channel_id TEXT,
   309	                event_hour_yf   TEXT,
   310	                call_datetime_utc TEXT,
   311	                call_source     TEXT,
   312	                created_at      TEXT    NOT NULL DEFAULT (datetime('now')),
   313	                updated_at      TEXT    NOT NULL DEFAULT (datetime('now')),
   314	                UNIQUE(ticker, event_date)
   315	            )
   316	        """)
   317	
   318	        # Create all other tables
   319	        for sql_list in _MIGRATIONS.values():
   320	            for sql in sql_list:
   321	                if sql.strip().upper().startswith("CREATE TABLE"):
   322	                    try:
   323	                        conn.execute(sql)
   324	                    except sqlite3.OperationalError:
   325	                        pass  # Already exists
   326	
   327	        _set_schema_version(conn, CURRENT_SCHEMA_VERSION)
   328	        conn.commit()
   329	        logger.info(f"Created fresh database at schema version {CURRENT_SCHEMA_VERSION}")
   330	    elif current_version < CURRENT_SCHEMA_VERSION:
   331	        _run_migrations(conn, current_version)
   332	    else:
   333	        logger.debug(f"Database at schema version {current_version}, no migrations needed")
   334	
   335	    return conn
   336

   338	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   339	# Event queries
   340	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   341	
   342	
   343	def find_existing_event(conn: sqlite3.Connection, ticker: str, event_date: str) -> dict | None:
   344	    """Look up an existing event by ticker + event_date. Returns dict or None."""
   345	    cur = conn.execute(
   346	        "SELECT id, ticker, quarter, event_date, event_hour, gcal_id, "
   347	        "eps_estimate, eps_actual, rev_estimate, rev_actual, reported, "
   348	        "tier, company_name, ticktick_task_id, date_locked, date_confirmed, "
   349	        "event_hour_yf, call_datetime_utc, call_source "
   350	        "FROM events WHERE ticker = ? AND event_date = ?",
   351	        (ticker, event_date),
   352	    )
   353	    row = cur.fetchone()
   354	    if row:
   355	        return {
   356	            "id": row[0], "ticker": row[1], "quarter": row[2],
   357	            "event_date": row[3], "event_hour": row[4], "gcal_id": row[5],
   358	            "eps_estimate": row[6], "eps_actual": row[7],
   359	            "rev_estimate": row[8], "rev_actual": row[9],
   360	            "reported": bool(row[10]), "tier": row[11],
   361	            "company_name": row[12], "ticktick_task_id": row[13],
   362	            "date_locked": bool(row[14]),
   363	            "date_confirmed": bool(row[15]),
   364	            "event_hour_yf": row[16],
   365	            "call_datetime_utc": row[17],
   366	            "call_source": row[18],
   367	        }
   368	    return None
   369	
   370	
   371	def find_event_by_ticker_quarter(conn: sqlite3.Connection, ticker: str, quarter: str) -> dict | None:
   372	    """Legacy lookup by ticker + quarter (for backward compatibility with old data)."""
   373	    cur = conn.execute(
   374	        "SELECT id, ticker, quarter, event_date, event_hour, gcal_id, "
   375	        "eps_estimate, eps_actual, rev_estimate, rev_actual, reported "
   376	        "FROM events WHERE ticker = ? AND quarter = ?",
   377	        (ticker, quarter),
   378	    )
   379	    row = cur.fetchone()
   380	    if row:
   381	        return {
   382	            "id": row[0], "ticker": row[1], "quarter": row[2],
   383	            "event_date": row[3], "event_hour": row[4], "gcal_id": row[5],
   384	            "eps_estimate": row[6], "eps_actual": row[7],
   385	            "rev_estimate": row[8], "rev_actual": row[9],
   386	            "reported": bool(row[10]),
   387	        }
   388	    return None
   389	
   390	
   391	def find_reported_event_for_quarter(
   392	    conn: sqlite3.Connection, ticker: str, quarter: str
   393	) -> dict | None:
   394	    """
   395	    Return an already-reported (reported=1) event for this ticker+reporting
   396	    quarter, if one exists. Used to suppress duplicate / phantom Finnhub
   397	    listings: once a company's quarter has been recorded with actuals and
   398	    posted, a second Finnhub entry for the same quarter at a *different* date
   399	    (a date-flapping forward listing, or a same-quarter duplicate row) is
   400	    noise — processing it re-posts the actuals and churns the calendar.
   401	    """
   402	    cur = conn.execute(
   403	        "SELECT event_date, eps_actual, rev_actual FROM events "
   404	        "WHERE ticker = ? AND quarter = ? AND reported = 1 "
   405	        "ORDER BY event_date LIMIT 1",
   406	        (ticker, quarter),
   407	    )
   408	    row = cur.fetchone()
   409	    if row:
   410	        return {"event_date": row[0], "eps_actual": row[1], "rev_actual": row[2]}
   411	    return None
   412

   418	    Find an existing event for a ticker within a date window.
   419	    Useful when Finnhub reports a slightly different date for the same earnings event.
   420	    """

   556	
   557	def _short_company_name(name: str) -> str:
   558	    """Trim trailing corporate suffixes for compact display."""
   559	    if not name:
   560	        return ""
   561	    s = name.strip()
   562	    suffixes = (
   563	        ", Inc.", ", Inc", " Inc.", " Inc", " Incorporated",
   564	        " Corp.", " Corp", " Corporation",
   565	        " Co., Ltd.", " Co Ltd", " Company",
   566	        " Ltd.", " Ltd", " Limited",
   567	        " plc", " PLC", " AG", " SA", " S.A.", " N.V.", " NV",
   568	        " Holdings", " Holding", " Group",
   569	    )
   570	    changed = True
   571	    while changed:
   572	        changed = False
   573	        for suf in suffixes:
   574	            if s.endswith(suf):
   575	                s = s[: -len(suf)].rstrip(",.& ")
   576	                changed = True
   577	                break
   578	    # Strip trailing connectors left behind ("Eli Lilly and Company" -> "Eli Lilly")
   579	    while True:
   580	        lowered = s.lower()
   581	        if lowered.endswith(" and"):
   582	            s = s[: -4].rstrip(",.& ")
   583	        elif lowered.endswith(" &"):
   584	            s = s[: -2].rstrip(",.& ")
   585	        else:
   586	            break
   587	    return s or name
   588	
   589	
   590	def _signed_pct(actual: float | None, estimate: float | None) -> str:
   591	    """Inline beat/miss tag: '+2.4%' / '(1.7%)' / '–' when N/A.
   592	
   593	    Color marker is rendered separately at the start of the line by
   594	    `_format_results_line` so the three per-row markers align in one column.
   595	    """
   596	    pct = _beat_miss_pct(actual, estimate)
   597	    if pct is None:
   598	        return "–"
   599	    if pct < 0:
   600	        return f"({abs(pct):.1f}%)"
   601	    return f"+{pct:.1f}%"
   602	
   603	
   604	def _fmt_eps_compact(actual: float | None, estimate: float | None) -> str:
   605	    a = _fmt_estimate_eps(actual) if actual is not None else "–"
   606	    e = _fmt_estimate_eps(estimate) if estimate is not None else "–"
   607	    return f"EPS {a}/{e} {_signed_pct(actual, estimate)}"
   608

   612	    e = _fmt_estimate_rev(estimate) if estimate is not None else "–"
   613	    return f"Rev {a}/{e} {_signed_pct(actual, estimate)}"

     1	"""
     2	Market data helpers — wraps yfinance for price performance queries.
     3	
     4	Currently provides YTD percent change. Best-effort: individual tickers that
     5	yfinance cannot resolve (e.g., some foreign listings) return None so the
     6	caller can render "–" instead of failing the whole digest.
     7	"""
     8	
     9	from __future__ import annotations
    10	
    11	import io
    12	import logging
    13	from contextlib import redirect_stderr, redirect_stdout
    14	from dataclasses import dataclass
    15	from datetime import date, datetime, time, timedelta, timezone
    16	
    17	try:
    18	    from zoneinfo import ZoneInfo
    19	except ImportError:  # pragma: no cover - py<3.9 fallback
    20	    ZoneInfo = None
    21	
    22	import yfinance as yf
    23	
    24	logger = logging.getLogger("earnings_agent")
    25	
    26	
    27	@dataclass
    28	class PostEarningsMove:
    29	    move_pct: float
    30	    # Short human-readable label describing what the move represents, e.g.
    31	    # "close vs prior close" or "next-day close vs earnings-day close".
    32	    window_label: str
    33	
    34	
    35	def fetch_ytd_performance(tickers: list[str]) -> dict[str, float | None]:
    36	    """
    37	    Return {ticker: ytd_pct_change} for the given tickers. A missing or
    38	    failed ticker maps to None instead of raising.
    39	
    40	    Uses a single batched yfinance download to keep network overhead low.
    41	    """
    42	    if not tickers:
    43	        return {}
    44	
    45	    unique = sorted(set(t.upper() for t in tickers))
    46	    result: dict[str, float | None] = {t: None for t in unique}
    47	
    48	    # yfinance is chatty on stdout/stderr even with progress=False; silence both.
    49	    buf_out, buf_err = io.StringIO(), io.StringIO()
    50	    try:
    51	        with redirect_stdout(buf_out), redirect_stderr(buf_err):
    52	            data = yf.download(
    53	                tickers=unique,
    54	                period="ytd",
    55	                progress=False,
    56	                auto_adjust=True,
    57	                threads=True,
    58	                group_by="ticker",
    59	            )
    60	    except Exception as exc:
    61	        logger.warning(f"yfinance batch download failed: {exc}")
    62	        return result
    63	
    64	    if data is None or data.empty:
    65	        logger.warning("yfinance returned empty YTD dataset")
    66	        return result
    67	
    68	    # When multiple tickers are requested, columns are a MultiIndex:
    69	    #   top level = ticker, second level = field (Open/High/Low/Close/Volume).
    70	    # When only one ticker is requested, columns are flat.
    71	    for ticker in unique:
    72	        try:
    73	            if len(unique) == 1:
    74	                closes = data["Close"].dropna()
    75	            else:
    76	                closes = data[ticker]["Close"].dropna()
    77	            if closes.empty:
    78	                continue
    79	            first = float(closes.iloc[0])
    80	            last = float(closes.iloc[-1])
    81	            if first == 0:
    82	                continue
    83	            result[ticker] = (last - first) / first * 100
    84	        except (KeyError, IndexError, ValueError) as exc:
    85	            logger.debug(f"YTD unavailable for {ticker}: {exc}")
    86	
    87	    missing = [t for t, v in result.items() if v is None]
    88	    if missing:
    89	        logger.info(f"YTD missing for {len(missing)} tickers: {', '.join(missing[:8])}"
    90	                    + ("..." if len(missing) > 8 else ""))
    91	    return result
    92	
    93	
    94	def fetch_post_earnings_move(
    95	    ticker: str, earnings_date: str, timing: str | None
    96	) -> PostEarningsMove | None:
    97	    """
    98	    Compute the post-earnings stock reaction for a ticker.
    99	
   100	    BMO / DMH / unknown: move = close(earnings_date) / close(prior trading day) - 1
   101	        → captures the day-of reaction to a pre-market or intraday announcement.
   102	    AMC: move = close(next trading day) / close(earnings_date) - 1
   103	        → AMC reports land after close; the reaction is the next day.
   104	
   105	    Returns None if we don't yet have the closing prices needed (e.g. running
   106	    the check the same evening as an AMC report — next-day data doesn't exist
   107	    yet).
   108	    """
   109	    try:
   110	        ed = date.fromisoformat(earnings_date)
   111	    except ValueError:
   112	        return None
   113	
   114	    # Pull a window wide enough to cover weekends/holidays either side.
   115	    start = ed - timedelta(days=10)
   116	    end = ed + timedelta(days=10)
   117	
   118	    buf_out, buf_err = io.StringIO(), io.StringIO()
   119	    try:
   120	        with redirect_stdout(buf_out), redirect_stderr(buf_err):
   121	            hist = yf.Ticker(ticker).history(
   122	                start=start.isoformat(),
   123	                end=end.isoformat(),
   124	                auto_adjust=True,
   125	            )
   126	    except Exception as exc:
   127	        logger.debug(f"post-earnings move fetch failed for {ticker}: {exc}")
   128	        return None
   129	
   130	    if hist is None or hist.empty:
   131	        return None
   132	
   133	    closes = hist["Close"].dropna()
   134	    if closes.empty:
   135	        return None
   136	
   137	    # Normalize index to date objects for comparison.
   138	    idx_dates = [d.date() for d in closes.index.to_pydatetime()]
   139	
   140	    def _find_on_or_before(target: date) -> tuple[date, float] | None:
   141	        for d, px in sorted(zip(idx_dates, closes.values), reverse=True):
   142	            if d <= target:
   143	                return d, float(px)
   144	        return None
   145	
   146	    def _find_on_or_after(target: date) -> tuple[date, float] | None:
   147	        for d, px in zip(idx_dates, closes.values):
   148	            if d >= target:
   149	                return d, float(px)
   150	        return None
   151	
   152	    timing_l = (timing or "").lower()
   153	
   154	    if timing_l == "amc":
   155	        ref = _find_on_or_before(ed)
   156	        post = _find_on_or_after(ed + timedelta(days=1))
   157	        if not ref or not post or post[0] == ref[0]:
   158	            return None
   159	        ref_px, post_px = ref[1], post[1]
   160	        window_label = "next-day close vs earnings-day close"
   161	    else:
   162	        # BMO, DMH, or unknown timing
   163	        post = _find_on_or_after(ed)
   164	        if not post:
   165	            return None
   166	        ref = _find_on_or_before(post[0] - timedelta(days=1))
   167	        if not ref:
   168	            return None
   169	        ref_px, post_px = ref[1], post[1]
   170	        window_label = "earnings-day close vs prior close"
   171	
   172	    if ref_px == 0:
   173	        return None
   174	    move_pct = (post_px - ref_px) / ref_px * 100
   175	    return PostEarningsMove(move_pct=move_pct, window_label=window_label)
   176	
   177	
   178	def fetch_yfinance_earnings_date(ticker: str) -> list[date] | None:
   179	    """
   180	    Return yfinance's current earnings date(s) for a ticker as a list of
   181	    date objects. May be a single date or a [start, end] range when
   182	    yfinance has a window rather than a specific day. Returns None if
   183	    yfinance has no data or the call fails.
   184	
   185	    Used as a cheap sanity check on Finnhub's date. yfinance itself
   186	    scrapes Yahoo Finance and is imperfect — treat disagreements as
   187	    "please verify manually", not as an automatic override.
   188	    """
   189	    buf_out, buf_err = io.StringIO(), io.StringIO()
   190	    try:
   191	        with redirect_stdout(buf_out), redirect_stderr(buf_err):
   192	            cal = yf.Ticker(ticker).calendar
   193	    except Exception as exc:
   194	        logger.debug(f"yfinance calendar fetch failed for {ticker}: {exc}")
   195	        return None
   196	
   197	    if not cal:
   198	        return None
   199	
   200	    # yfinance typically returns a dict; handle DataFrame just in case
   201	    if isinstance(cal, dict):
   202	        raw = cal.get("Earnings Date")
   203	    elif hasattr(cal, "loc") and hasattr(cal, "index"):
   204	        if "Earnings Date" not in cal.index:
   205	            return None
   206	        try:
   207	            raw = cal.loc["Earnings Date"].values.tolist()
   208	        except Exception:
   209	            return None
   210	    else:
   211	        return None
   212	
   213	    if raw is None:
   214	        return None
   215	    if not isinstance(raw, (list, tuple)):
   216	        raw = [raw]
   217	
   218	    result: list[date] = []
   219	    for d in raw:
   220	        if isinstance(d, date):
   221	            result.append(d)
   222	        elif hasattr(d, "date"):
   223	            result.append(d.date())
   224	        else:
   225	            try:
   226	                result.append(date.fromisoformat(str(d)[:10]))
   227	            except (ValueError, TypeError):
   228	                continue
   229	    return result or None
   230	
   231	
   232	@dataclass
   233	class YfinanceEarningsTimestamps:
   234	    """yfinance earnings-timing fields, distinguished by event type.
   235	
   236	    The press release and the conference call are distinct events that
   237	    sometimes happen on different calendar days (e.g. UFPT: AMC release
   238	    on Monday, BMO call on Tuesday). The calendar tracks the press
   239	    release; the call is descriptive context. Keep them separate so
   240	    callers don't conflate them.

   269	            "elements": [
   270	                {
   271	                    "type": "mrkdwn",
   272	                    "text": (
   273	                        f"Through {week_end_str} · "
   274	                        f"{digest.month_tracked_count} tracked names in next 30 days"
   275	                    ),
   276	                }
   277	            ],
   278	        },
   279	        {"type": "divider"},
   280	    ]
   281	
   282	    for block in (
   283	        _slack_tier_block("Core Watchlist", digest.tier1_week, show_company=True),
   284	        _slack_tier_block("HC Services + MedTech", digest.tier2_week, show_company=True),
   285	        _slack_tier_block("Other", digest.tier3_week, show_company=True),
   286	    ):
   287	        if block:
   288	            blocks.append(block)
   289	
   290	    ctx = _slack_context_block(digest)
   291	    if ctx:
   292	        blocks.append({"type": "divider"})
   293	        blocks.append(ctx)
   294	
   295	    if len(blocks) > SLACK_MAX_BLOCKS:
   296	        blocks = blocks[:SLACK_MAX_BLOCKS]
   297	    return blocks
   298	
   299	
   300	def post_slack(webhook_url: str, blocks: list[dict], fallback_text: str) -> None:
   301	    """POST a Block Kit message. Raises NotificationError on failure."""
   302	    payload = {"text": fallback_text, "blocks": blocks}
   303	    try:
   304	        # Retry transient network blips; non-200 handling stays below unchanged.
   305	        resp = post_with_retry(
   306	            webhook_url,
   307	            data=json.dumps(payload),
   308	            headers={"Content-Type": "application/json"},
   309	            timeout=SLACK_TIMEOUT,
   310	            label="Slack webhook",
   311	        )
   312	    except requests.RequestException as exc:
   313	        raise NotificationError(f"Slack POST failed: {exc}") from exc
   314	
   315	    if resp.status_code != 200 or resp.text.strip() != "ok":
   316	        raise NotificationError(
   317	            f"Slack webhook returned {resp.status_code}: {resp.text[:200]}"
   318	        )
   319	    logger.info("Slack message posted successfully")
   320	
   321	
   322	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   323	# Email rendering
   324	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

   326	
   327	def _row_table_html(rows: list[EventRow], show_estimates: bool) -> str:
   328	    if not rows:
   329	        return "<p><em>None</em></p>"
   330	    header_cols = "<th>Ticker</th><th>Company</th><th>Date</th><th>Timing</th>"

   785	# kv_store (v9) — generic config that can be mutated via Slack reply

   788	
   789	def kv_get(conn: sqlite3.Connection, key: str) -> str | None:
   790	    cur = conn.execute("SELECT value FROM kv_store WHERE key = ?", (key,))
   791	    row = cur.fetchone()
   792	    return row[0] if row else None
   793	
   794	
   795	def kv_set(conn: sqlite3.Connection, key: str, value: str) -> None:
   796	    conn.execute(
   797	        "INSERT INTO kv_store (key, value, updated_at) "
   798	        "VALUES (?, ?, datetime('now')) "
   799	        "ON CONFLICT(key) DO UPDATE SET "
   800	        "value = excluded.value, updated_at = excluded.updated_at",
   801	        (key, value),
   802	    )
   803	    conn.commit()
   804	
   805	
   806	def kv_list_prefix(conn: sqlite3.Connection, prefix: str) -> dict[str, str]:
   807	    cur = conn.execute(
   808	        "SELECT key, value FROM kv_store WHERE key LIKE ? ORDER BY key",
   809	        (prefix + "%",),
   810	    )
   811	    return {row[0]: row[1] for row in cur.fetchall()}

/bin/bash -lc "nl -ba coverage.py | sed -n '1,220p'" in /mnt/c/Users/jroyp/Dropbox/Claude Folder/earnings_agent
 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	"""
     2	Coverage Manager integration — reads the canonical ticker universe and
     3	resolves each ticker to a service tier.
     4	
     5	Tier 1 (Top priority — held + actively researched + trigger-ready):
     6	    - Portfolio + Researching ∩ Core (held names + active thesis work)
     7	    - Ready to Buy + Ready to Short (trigger-ready; Core filter dropped
     8	      because user explicitly committed by completing the thesis)
     9	Tier 2 (HC Services + MedTech): universe tickers in those sectors, excluding Tier 1
    10	Tier 3 (Other): everything else in the universe
    11	
    12	The TickerInfo.position field carries the original Position state for any
    13	ticker in one of the five Position lists (Portfolio / Researching /
    14	Ready to Buy / Ready to Short / Following for Interest), regardless of
    15	which tier the ticker landed in. Following for Interest names keep their
    16	sector-derived tier (no automatic promotion to Tier 1) but still get a
    17	non-empty .position so the digest can render them under their own
    18	subgroup. notifications._subgroup uses .position before falling back to
    19	sector-based bucketing.
    20	
    21	Falls back to legacy core_watchlist.json (= Portfolio + Researching unioned)
    22	during the Coverage Manager Phase B->C migration window.
    23	"""
    24	
    25	import csv
    26	import json
    27	import logging
    28	from datetime import datetime, timezone
    29	from pathlib import Path
    30	from dataclasses import dataclass
    31	
    32	from config import COVERAGE_MANAGER_PATH, TIER_2_SECTORS, TICKERS_FILE
    33	
    34	logger = logging.getLogger("earnings_agent")
    35	
    36	
    37	# Coverage Manager publishes weekly (Friday Windows Task Scheduler), so a
    38	# healthy manifest age oscillates 0–7 days. The threshold must give that
    39	# cadence slack: Friday's publish time drifts (06-05 landed ~11:00 UTC,
    40	# 06-12 ~20:40 UTC) and the staleness check runs on the morning daily sync
    41	# (11:13 UTC) + watchdog (13:37 UTC) — i.e. BEFORE Friday's evening publish.
    42	# A flat 7d threshold therefore false-alarmed every Friday morning for the
    43	# hours between crossing 7.0d and that day's publish (the 2026-06-12 alert).
    44	# 10d cleanly separates a normal/slightly-late weekly publish (≤~7.5d) from a
    45	# genuinely missed week (reaches 10d ~3 days after the skipped Friday — still
    46	# a within-72h alert), which is the "a real miss is loud" intent. CM's
    47	# manifest.json carries `generated_at` (ISO Z); fall back to universe.csv
    48	# mtime if the manifest is missing.
    49	COVERAGE_STALENESS_DAYS = 10
    50	
    51	
    52	@dataclass
    53	class TickerInfo:
    54	    ticker: str
    55	    tier: int               # 1, 2, or 3
    56	    company_name: str
    57	    sector: str
    58	    subsector: str
    59	    # One of the five Position values from Coverage Manager, or "" for
    60	    # tickers not in any Position list. Drives digest subgrouping in
    61	    # notifications._subgroup. Expanded 2026-05-11 from {Portfolio,
    62	    # Researching} to all five values.
    63	    position: str = ""      # "Portfolio" | "Researching" | "Ready to Buy" | "Ready to Short" | "Following for Interest" | ""
    64	
    65	
    66	@dataclass
    67	class CoverageHealth:
    68	    """Result of compute_coverage_freshness — pure data, no side effects."""
    69	    stale: bool
    70	    age_days: float | None
    71	    source: str            # "manifest", "mtime", or "missing"
    72	    message: str           # human-readable summary for logs/Slack
    73	
    74	
    75	def compute_coverage_freshness() -> CoverageHealth:
    76	    """Inspect Coverage Manager exports for staleness. Pure read — no DB,
    77	    no Slack, no logger.warning side-effects (callers decide).
    78	
    79	    Preference order:
    80	      1. exports/manifest.json -> 'generated_at' field (canonical)
    81	      2. exports/universe.csv mtime (fallback if manifest absent or malformed)
    82	      3. neither -> stale=True, source='missing'
    83	    """
    84	    exports = Path(COVERAGE_MANAGER_PATH) / "exports"
    85	    manifest = exports / "manifest.json"
    86	    universe = exports / "universe.csv"
    87	    now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
    88	
    89	    if manifest.exists():
    90	        try:
    91	            with open(manifest, encoding="utf-8") as f:
    92	                data = json.load(f)
    93	            ts = data.get("generated_at")
    94	            if ts:
    95	                # CM publishes "...Z" suffix; fromisoformat doesn't accept Z
    96	                # before Python 3.11. Normalize defensively.
    97	                ts_clean = ts.replace("Z", "+00:00") if ts.endswith("Z") else ts
    98	                generated = datetime.fromisoformat(ts_clean)
    99	                if generated.tzinfo is None:
   100	                    generated = generated.replace(tzinfo=timezone.utc)
   101	                age_days = (now - generated).total_seconds() / 86400
   102	                stale = age_days > COVERAGE_STALENESS_DAYS
   103	                msg = (
   104	                    f"Coverage Manager exports generated_at={ts}; "
   105	                    f"age={age_days:.1f}d (threshold {COVERAGE_STALENESS_DAYS}d)"
   106	                )
   107	                return CoverageHealth(stale=stale, age_days=age_days, source="manifest", message=msg)
   108	        except (json.JSONDecodeError, ValueError, OSError) as exc:
   109	            logger.debug(f"Manifest unparseable, falling back to mtime: {exc}")
   110	
   111	    if universe.exists():
   112	        age_days = (now.timestamp() - universe.stat().st_mtime) / 86400
   113	        stale = age_days > COVERAGE_STALENESS_DAYS
   114	        msg = (
   115	            f"Coverage Manager universe.csv mtime age={age_days:.1f}d "
   116	            f"(threshold {COVERAGE_STALENESS_DAYS}d) — manifest unavailable"
   117	        )
   118	        return CoverageHealth(stale=stale, age_days=age_days, source="mtime", message=msg)
   119	
   120	    return CoverageHealth(
   121	        stale=True, age_days=None, source="missing",
   122	        message=f"Coverage Manager exports not found at {exports}",
   123	    )
   124	
   125	
   126	def _read_position_json(exports_path: Path, filename: str) -> dict[str, dict]:
   127	    """Read portfolio.json or researching.json, return {TICKER: row dict}."""
   128	    path = exports_path / filename
   129	    if not path.exists():
   130	        return {}
   131	    try:
   132	        with open(path, encoding="utf-8") as f:
   133	            data = json.load(f)
   134	    except (json.JSONDecodeError, OSError) as e:
   135	        logger.warning(f"Could not read {filename}: {e}")
   136	        return {}
   137	    if not isinstance(data, dict):
   138	        return {}
   139	    return {t.strip().upper(): row for t, row in data.items() if isinstance(row, dict)}
   140	
   141	
   142	def _read_position_lists(exports_path: Path) -> dict[str, dict[str, dict]]:
   143	    """Read all five Position files and return a {label: {ticker: row}} dict.
   144	
   145	    Returns an empty inner dict for any file that's absent. Falls back to
   146	    legacy watchlist.csv when none of the five new files are present
   147	    (Coverage Manager Phase B->C migration window) — in that case the
   148	    legacy union is returned under "Portfolio" only and the other four
   149	    labels stay empty.
   150	
   151	    Tier-1 promotion rules are applied by the caller, not here:
   152	      - Portfolio + Researching require Core=Y for Tier 1 (legacy rule).
   153	      - Ready to Buy + Ready to Short are Tier 1 unconditionally
   154	        (trigger-ready ⇒ user committed).
   155	      - Following for Interest is NOT auto-promoted; falls through to
   156	        sector-based tiering.
   157	
   158	    This function just surfaces the raw lists. Filter/promotion logic
   159	    lives in load_coverage.
   160	    """
   161	    lists = {
   162	        "Portfolio": _read_position_json(exports_path, "portfolio.json"),
   163	        "Researching": _read_position_json(exports_path, "researching.json"),
   164	        "Following for Interest": _read_position_json(exports_path, "following_for_interest.json"),
   165	        "Ready to Buy": _read_position_json(exports_path, "ready_to_buy.json"),
   166	        "Ready to Short": _read_position_json(exports_path, "ready_to_short.json"),
   167	    }
   168	
   169	    if not any(lists.values()):
   170	        # Legacy fallback: read watchlist.csv (Portfolio + Researching unioned)
   171	        # and treat everything as Portfolio for the migration window.
   172	        watchlist_path = exports_path / "watchlist.csv"
   173	        if not watchlist_path.exists():
   174	            logger.warning(f"Neither position files nor legacy watchlist found at {exports_path}")
   175	            return lists
   176	        with open(watchlist_path, newline="", encoding="utf-8") as f:
   177	            for row in csv.DictReader(f):
   178	                if row.get("Core", "").strip().upper() == "Y":
   179	                    ticker = row.get("Ticker", "").strip().upper()
   180	                    if ticker:
   181	                        lists["Portfolio"][ticker] = row
   182	
   183	    return lists
   184	
   185	
   186	def _read_universe_metadata(exports_path: Path) -> dict[str, dict]:
   187	    """Read universe_metadata.json and return dict of ticker -> {name, sector, subsector}."""
   188	    metadata_path = exports_path / "universe_metadata.json"
   189	    if not metadata_path.exists():
   190	        logger.warning(f"Universe metadata not found: {metadata_path}")
   191	        return {}
   192	
   193	    with open(metadata_path, encoding="utf-8") as f:
   194	        raw = json.load(f)
   195	
   196	    # Keys in the JSON may not have exchange suffixes — normalize to uppercase
   197	    result = {}
   198	    for ticker, info in raw.items():
   199	        key = ticker.strip().upper()
   200	        result[key] = info
   201	    return result
   202	
   203	
   204	def _read_universe_tickers(exports_path: Path) -> set[str]:
   205	    """Read universe.csv and return set of all tickers."""
   206	    universe_path = exports_path / "universe.csv"
   207	    if not universe_path.exists():
   208	        logger.warning(f"Universe not found: {universe_path}")
   209	        return set()
   210	
   211	    tickers = set()
   212	    with open(universe_path, newline="", encoding="utf-8") as f:
   213	        for row in csv.DictReader(f):
   214	            ticker = row.get("Ticker", "").strip().upper()
   215	            if ticker:
   216	                tickers.add(ticker)
   217	    return tickers

   219	
   220	def _load_legacy_tickers() -> list[str]:

exec
/bin/bash -lc "nl -ba fmp_client.py | sed -n '1,220p'" in /mnt/c/Users/jroyp/Dropbox/Claude Folder/earnings_agent
 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	"""
     2	FMP earnings-calendar client + Finnhub/FMP merge.
     3	
     4	Why this exists: a universe-wide comparison (scripts/compare_providers.py) showed
     5	FMP — which we already pay for via Coverage Manager's Starter plan — covers far
     6	more of our names per window than Finnhub's free tier (≈+14 Tier-1 / +70 Tier-2
     7	reporters, almost all WITH actuals) and is never behind on actuals (it had
     8	actuals for 30 names Finnhub lacked, incl. FIVE; the reverse was 0). Date
     9	accuracy between the two is a wash, and FMP actually carries MORE phantom
    10	double-listings, so the design is deliberately a *merge*, not a replacement:
    11	
    12	  - Finnhub stays the date authority on names BOTH sources have (its date is
    13	    what the calendar is anchored to; date conflicts are arbitrated by the
    14	    existing yfinance/EDGAR cross-check, not here) — this sidesteps FMP's
    15	    occasional date errors on shared names.
    16	  - FMP fills the gaps: names Finnhub never lists (breadth) and actuals
    17	    Finnhub hasn't ingested yet (timeliness).
    18	  - The same-quarter phantom guard downstream (storage/main) still applies, so
    19	    FMP's extra phantoms can't reintroduce the re-post bug.
    20	
    21	Output is normalized to Finnhub's event shape so the rest of the agent is
    22	unchanged: dicts with keys symbol, date, hour, epsEstimate, epsActual,
    23	revenueEstimate, revenueActual (+ a 'source' tag for observability).
    24	"""
    25	import json
    26	import logging
    27	import time
    28	import urllib.request
    29	import urllib.error
    30	from collections import defaultdict
    31	from dataclasses import dataclass
    32	from datetime import date, timedelta
    33	
    34	from config import FMP_API_KEY
    35	from storage import date_to_quarter
    36	
    37	logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)
    38	
    39	
    40	@dataclass
    41	class FMPFetch:
    42	    """Result of a chunked FMP fetch, carrying partial-failure counts so the
    43	    caller can alarm on silent coverage loss (some chunks failed but the run
    44	    still looks healthy)."""
    45	    events: list
    46	    failed_chunks: int
    47	    total_chunks: int
    48	
    49	_FMP_BASE = "https://financialmodelingprep.com/stable/earnings-calendar"
    50	_CHUNK_DAYS = 7          # weekly chunks dodge any server-side range cap
    51	_CHUNK_SLEEP = 0.25
    52	
    53	
    54	def _normalize(row: dict) -> dict | None:
    55	    """FMP bulk row -> Finnhub-shaped event dict (or None if unusable)."""
    56	    sym = (row.get("symbol") or "").upper()
    57	    d = row.get("date")
    58	    if not sym or not d:
    59	        return None
    60	    return {
    61	        "symbol": sym,
    62	        "date": d[:10],
    63	        "hour": None,  # FMP bulk carries no BMO/AMC; yfinance fallback fills it
    64	        "epsEstimate": row.get("epsEstimated"),
    65	        "epsActual": row.get("epsActual"),
    66	        "revenueEstimate": row.get("revenueEstimated"),
    67	        "revenueActual": row.get("revenueActual"),
    68	        "source": "fmp",
    69	    }
    70	
    71	
    72	def fetch_fmp_earnings(
    73	    tickers, from_iso: str, to_iso: str, *, timeout: int = 30
    74	) -> FMPFetch:
    75	    """Fetch the FMP earnings calendar over [from_iso, to_iso], filtered to
    76	    `tickers`, normalized to Finnhub's event shape. Chunked weekly.
    77	
    78	    Returns an FMPFetch carrying the events plus failed/total chunk counts so a
    79	    PARTIAL outage (some chunks failed) is observable rather than silently
    80	    shrinking the merge. Raises only on a hard/auth failure (401/403, or an
    81	    error payload), which the caller treats as a full FMP outage and degrades
    82	    to Finnhub-only.
    83	    """
    84	    if not FMP_API_KEY:
    85	        raise RuntimeError("FMP_API_KEY not configured")
    86	
    87	    universe = {t.upper() for t in tickers}
    88	    out: list[dict] = []
    89	    start = date.fromisoformat(from_iso)
    90	    end = date.fromisoformat(to_iso)
    91	    cur = start
    92	    total_chunks = 0
    93	    failed_chunks = 0
    94	    while cur <= end:
    95	        chunk_end = min(cur + timedelta(days=_CHUNK_DAYS - 1), end)
    96	        total_chunks += 1
    97	        url = (
    98	            f"{_FMP_BASE}?from={cur.isoformat()}&to={chunk_end.isoformat()}"
    99	            f"&apikey={FMP_API_KEY}"
   100	        )
   101	        try:
   102	            with urllib.request.urlopen(url, timeout=timeout) as resp:
   103	                data = json.load(resp)
   104	        except urllib.error.HTTPError as exc:
   105	            # 401/403 = auth/plan problem: hard-fail so the caller degrades
   106	            # loudly rather than silently dropping FMP coverage every run.
   107	            if exc.code in (401, 403):
   108	                raise RuntimeError(f"FMP auth/plan error {exc.code}: {exc.reason}")
   109	            logger.warning(f"FMP chunk {cur}..{chunk_end} HTTP {exc.code}; skipping")
   110	            failed_chunks += 1
   111	            cur = chunk_end + timedelta(days=1)
   112	            continue
   113	        except Exception as exc:
   114	            logger.warning(f"FMP chunk {cur}..{chunk_end} error: {exc}; skipping")
   115	            failed_chunks += 1
   116	            cur = chunk_end + timedelta(days=1)
   117	            continue
   118	
   119	        if isinstance(data, dict):
   120	            # FMP returns an {"Error Message": ...} dict on plan/endpoint issues.
   121	            raise RuntimeError(f"FMP returned error payload: {str(data)[:160]}")
   122	        for row in data:
   123	            if (row.get("symbol") or "").upper() not in universe:
   124	                continue
   125	            ev = _normalize(row)
   126	            if ev:
   127	                out.append(ev)
   128	        cur = chunk_end + timedelta(days=1)
   129	        time.sleep(_CHUNK_SLEEP)
   130	
   131	    level = logger.warning if failed_chunks else logger.info
   132	    level(
   133	        f"FMP earnings: {len(out)} universe events over "
   134	        f"{total_chunks - failed_chunks}/{total_chunks} chunk(s)"
   135	        + (f" ({failed_chunks} FAILED)" if failed_chunks else "")
   136	    )
   137	    return FMPFetch(events=out, failed_chunks=failed_chunks, total_chunks=total_chunks)
   138	
   139	
   140	def _has_actuals(ev: dict) -> bool:
   141	    return ev.get("epsActual") is not None or ev.get("revenueActual") is not None
   142	
   143	
   144	def _fill_from(primary: dict, donor: dict) -> dict:
   145	    """Return primary with missing est/actual fields — and the earnings hour —
   146	    filled from donor.
   147	
   148	    Preserving `hour` matters: FMP rows carry hour=None, so when an FMP actuals
   149	    row WINS over a Finnhub row that knew the session (e.g. Finnhub had `amc`
   150	    but no actuals yet), dropping the hour would mislead
   151	    `fetch_post_earnings_move` (which treats amc vs bmo/unknown differently for
   152	    the move window + deferral). So inherit the donor's hour when the chosen
   153	    row lacks one.
   154	    """
   155	    merged = dict(primary)
   156	    for k in ("epsEstimate", "epsActual", "revenueEstimate", "revenueActual"):
   157	        if merged.get(k) is None and donor.get(k) is not None:
   158	            merged[k] = donor[k]
   159	    if not merged.get("hour") and donor.get("hour"):
   160	        merged["hour"] = donor["hour"]
   161	    # Note both contributors for observability.
   162	    srcs = {primary.get("source", "finnhub"), donor.get("source", "finnhub")}
   163	    merged["source"] = "+".join(sorted(srcs))
   164	    return merged
   165	
   166	
   167	def merge_earnings(fh_events: list[dict], fmp_events: list[dict]) -> list[dict]:
   168	    """Merge Finnhub + FMP events into one Finnhub-shaped list.
   169	
   170	    Policy, per (ticker, reporting-quarter):
   171	      1. Finnhub has actuals          -> use Finnhub row, fill gaps from FMP.
   172	      2. Finnhub has it but NO actuals
   173	         and FMP HAS actuals          -> use FMP row (its date is the real
   174	                                          report date; fixes the FIVE lag),
   175	                                          fill estimates from Finnhub.
   176	      3. Both upcoming (no actuals)    -> use Finnhub row (date authority),
   177	                                          fill estimates from FMP.
   178	      4. Only one source has it        -> take that one (breadth win, ~all FMP).
   179	
   180	    Row-count behaviour, to be precise:
   181	      - Single-source (ticker, quarter): ALL of that source's rows pass through
   182	        intact (so e.g. a Finnhub same-quarter phantom + real row both reach
   183	        the downstream same-quarter phantom guard, which collapses them).
   184	      - Both-source (ticker, quarter): collapses to ONE representative row
   185	        (picked per the policy above, gaps filled from the other source). The
   186	        downstream guard still protects against phantoms that surface across
   187	        runs / against persisted DB state, so cross-source extras don't need to
   188	        pass through here.
   189	    """
   190	    for e in fh_events:
   191	        e.setdefault("source", "finnhub")
   192	
   193	    fh_by_key: dict[tuple, list[dict]] = defaultdict(list)
   194	    fmp_by_key: dict[tuple, list[dict]] = defaultdict(list)
   195	    for e in fh_events:
   196	        fh_by_key[(e["symbol"], date_to_quarter(e["date"]))].append(e)
   197	    for e in fmp_events:
   198	        fmp_by_key[(e["symbol"], date_to_quarter(e["date"]))].append(e)
   199	
   200	    out: list[dict] = []
   201	    for key in set(fh_by_key) | set(fmp_by_key):
   202	        fh_rows = fh_by_key.get(key, [])
   203	        fmp_rows = fmp_by_key.get(key, [])
   204	
   205	        if fh_rows and not fmp_rows:
   206	            out.extend(fh_rows)
   207	            continue
   208	        if fmp_rows and not fh_rows:
   209	            out.extend(fmp_rows)
   210	            continue
   211	
   212	        # Both sources have this (ticker, quarter). Pick representative rows.
   213	        fh_act = next((r for r in fh_rows if _has_actuals(r)), None)
   214	        fmp_act = next((r for r in fmp_rows if _has_actuals(r)), None)
   215	
   216	        if fh_act:                                   # (1) Finnhub reported
   217	            out.append(_fill_from(fh_act, fmp_act or fmp_rows[0]))
   218	        elif fmp_act:                                # (2) only FMP reported
   219	            out.append(_fill_from(fmp_act, fh_rows[0]))
   220	        else:                                        # (3) both upcoming

exec

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	"""
     2	Finnhub API client — earnings calendar queries with chunking,
     3	retry with exponential backoff, and specific exception handling.
     4	"""
     5	
     6	import time
     7	import logging
     8	from datetime import date, timedelta
     9	
    10	import finnhub
    11	from requests.exceptions import RequestException, Timeout, ConnectionError as ReqConnectionError
    12	
    13	from config import (
    14	    FINNHUB_API_KEY,
    15	    CHUNK_DAYS,
    16	    CHUNK_SLEEP,
    17	    FINNHUB_MAX_RESULTS,
    18	    RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS,
    19	    RETRY_BASE_DELAY,
    20	)
    21	
    22	logger = logging.getLogger("earnings_agent")
    23	
    24	
    25	class FinnhubError(Exception):
    26	    """Raised when Finnhub API returns an error we can't retry."""
    27	    pass
    28	
    29	
    30	def _retry(func, *args, **kwargs):
    31	    """
    32	    Retry a function with exponential backoff.
    33	    Retries on transient network errors and rate limits.
    34	    """
    35	    last_exc = None
    36	    for attempt in range(1, RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS + 1):
    37	        try:
    38	            return func(*args, **kwargs)
    39	        except (Timeout, ReqConnectionError) as exc:
    40	            last_exc = exc
    41	            if attempt < RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS:
    42	                delay = RETRY_BASE_DELAY * (2 ** (attempt - 1))
    43	                logger.warning(
    44	                    f"Transient error (attempt {attempt}/{RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS}): {exc}. "
    45	                    f"Retrying in {delay}s..."
    46	                )
    47	                time.sleep(delay)
    48	        except finnhub.FinnhubAPIException as exc:
    49	            # Rate limit (429) is retryable; other API errors are not
    50	            if "429" in str(exc) or "rate limit" in str(exc).lower():
    51	                last_exc = exc
    52	                if attempt < RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS:
    53	                    delay = RETRY_BASE_DELAY * (2 ** (attempt - 1))
    54	                    logger.warning(
    55	                        f"Rate limited (attempt {attempt}/{RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS}). "
    56	                        f"Retrying in {delay}s..."
    57	                    )
    58	                    time.sleep(delay)
    59	            else:
    60	                raise FinnhubError(f"Finnhub API error: {exc}") from exc
    61	        except RequestException as exc:
    62	            last_exc = exc
    63	            if attempt < RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS:
    64	                delay = RETRY_BASE_DELAY * (2 ** (attempt - 1))
    65	                logger.warning(
    66	                    f"Request error (attempt {attempt}/{RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS}): {exc}. "
    67	                    f"Retrying in {delay}s..."
    68	                )
    69	                time.sleep(delay)
    70	
    71	    raise FinnhubError(f"Failed after {RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS} attempts: {last_exc}") from last_exc
    72	
    73	
    74	def get_client() -> finnhub.Client:
    75	    """Create a Finnhub API client."""
    76	    if not FINNHUB_API_KEY:
    77	        raise FinnhubError("FINNHUB_API_KEY not configured")
    78	    return finnhub.Client(api_key=FINNHUB_API_KEY)
    79	
    80	
    81	def _fetch_chunk(
    82	    client: finnhub.Client,
    83	    start: date,
    84	    end: date,
    85	    ticker_set: set[str],
    86	    depth: int = 0,
    87	) -> tuple[list[dict], int]:
    88	    """
    89	    Fetch a single date-range chunk, adaptively splitting on cap-hit.
    90	
    91	    Returns (matched_events, total_events_fetched_in_subtree).
    92	    Raises FinnhubError if the cap is still hit at 1-day granularity,
    93	    or if retries are exhausted inside _retry — both are run-aborting
    94	    conditions because continuing would yield silently-incomplete data.
    95	    """
    96	    span_days = (end - start).days
    97	    chunk_from = start.isoformat()
    98	    chunk_to = end.isoformat()
    99	
   100	    # _retry raises FinnhubError on exhausted retries. We let it propagate
   101	    # — swallowing here is what caused silent data loss.
   102	    result = _retry(
   103	        client.earnings_calendar,
   104	        _from=chunk_from,
   105	        to=chunk_to,
   106	        symbol="",
   107	        international=False,
   108	    )
   109	    all_earnings = result.get("earningsCalendar", [])
   110	    chunk_matches = [
   111	        e for e in all_earnings
   112	        if e.get("symbol", "").upper() in ticker_set
   113	    ]
   114	    indent = "  " * (depth + 1)
   115	    logger.info(
   116	        f"{indent}{chunk_from} -> {chunk_to} (span={span_days}d): "
   117	        f"{len(all_earnings)} total, {len(chunk_matches)} matched"
   118	    )
   119	
   120	    if len(all_earnings) < FINNHUB_MAX_RESULTS:
   121	        return chunk_matches, len(all_earnings)
   122	
   123	    # Cap hit. Finnhub silently truncated — we must re-fetch at smaller
   124	    # granularity or abort. A 1-day chunk at the cap means >= 1500 earnings
   125	    # reports in a single day, which shouldn't happen in our universe; if it
   126	    # does, we have no way to paginate and cannot trust completeness.
   127	    if span_days <= 1:
   128	        raise FinnhubError(
   129	            f"Finnhub cap ({FINNHUB_MAX_RESULTS}) hit at 1-day granularity "
   130	            f"for {chunk_from}. Cannot guarantee complete data — aborting."
   131	        )
   132	
   133	    mid = start + timedelta(days=max(span_days // 2, 1))
   134	    logger.warning(
   135	        f"{indent}Cap hit at {span_days}d span. Splitting at {mid.isoformat()}."
   136	    )
   137	    left_matched, left_total = _fetch_chunk(client, start, mid, ticker_set, depth + 1)
   138	    time.sleep(CHUNK_SLEEP)
   139	    right_matched, right_total = _fetch_chunk(client, mid, end, ticker_set, depth + 1)
   140	    return left_matched + right_matched, left_total + right_total
   141	
   142	
   143	def fetch_earnings(
   144	    client: finnhub.Client,
   145	    tickers: list[str],
   146	    from_date: str,
   147	    to_date: str,
   148	) -> list[dict]:
   149	    """
   150	    Query Finnhub earnings calendar in date-range chunks, filtering
   151	    client-side for our watchlist.
   152	
   153	    Chunks that hit Finnhub's 1500-result cap are adaptively split until
   154	    they clear or bottom out at 1-day granularity. If a 1-day chunk still
   155	    hits the cap, or any chunk's retries are exhausted, this function
   156	    raises FinnhubError — silent incomplete data is worse than a loud
   157	    failed run that fires the on-failure Slack alert.
   158	    """
   159	    logger.info(f"Querying Finnhub earnings calendar: {from_date} -> {to_date}")
   160	
   161	    ticker_set = {t.upper() for t in tickers}
   162	    start = date.fromisoformat(from_date)
   163	    end = date.fromisoformat(to_date)
   164	    matched: list[dict] = []
   165	    total_fetched = 0
   166	
   167	    while start < end:
   168	        chunk_end = min(start + timedelta(days=CHUNK_DAYS), end)
   169	        chunk_matched, chunk_total = _fetch_chunk(
   170	            client, start, chunk_end, ticker_set
   171	        )
   172	        matched.extend(chunk_matched)
   173	        total_fetched += chunk_total
   174	        start = chunk_end
   175	        time.sleep(CHUNK_SLEEP)
   176	
   177	    logger.info(
   178	        f"Scanned {total_fetched} total earnings across all chunks. "
   179	        f"Matched {len(matched)} events for {len(tickers)} tickers."
   180	    )

   444	def upsert_event(
   445	    conn: sqlite3.Connection,
   446	    ticker: str,
   447	    event_date: str,
   448	    event_hour: str | None,
   449	    gcal_id: str | None,
   450	    *,
   451	    quarter: str | None = None,
   452	    eps_estimate: float | None = None,
   453	    eps_actual: float | None = None,
   454	    rev_estimate: float | None = None,
   455	    rev_actual: float | None = None,
   456	    reported: bool = False,
   457	    tier: int = 3,
   458	    company_name: str | None = None,
   459	    source_fingerprint: str | None = None,
   460	    event_hour_yf: str | None = None,
   461	    call_datetime_utc: str | None = None,
   462	    call_source: str | None = None,
   463	):
   464	    """
   465	    Insert or update an event, keyed on (ticker, event_date).
   466	
   467	    The `date_confirmed` column is derived from `event_hour` (Finnhub-only):
   468	    Finnhub populates `bmo`/`amc`/`dmh` when the company has announced
   469	    timing, which in practice signals the date is confirmed.
   470	
   471	    `event_hour_yf` is a separate column carrying yfinance-inferred timing
   472	    used as a render fallback when Finnhub's `event_hour` is empty. It does
   473	    NOT flip `date_confirmed` — that flag stays Finnhub-canonical so
   474	    downstream cross-check messaging (notifications.py:_xcheck_verdict)
   475	    keeps "company-confirmed" semantics.
   476	
   477	    Pass `event_hour_yf=""` to explicitly clear it; pass `None` to leave
   478	    the existing value untouched (COALESCE preserves prior yfinance hits
   479	    across runs where yfinance has a transient failure).
   480	    """
   481	    if source_fingerprint is None:
   482	        source_fingerprint = f"{ticker}:{event_date}"
   483	
   484	    date_confirmed = int((event_hour or "").lower() in ("bmo", "amc", "dmh"))
   485	
   486	    # Try update first (handles both old UNIQUE(ticker, quarter) and new UNIQUE(ticker, event_date))
   487	    cur = conn.execute(
   488	        "SELECT id FROM events WHERE ticker = ? AND event_date = ?",
   489	        (ticker, event_date),
   490	    )
   491	    existing = cur.fetchone()
   492	
   493	    if existing:
   494	        conn.execute(
   495	            """
   496	            UPDATE events SET
   497	                event_hour        = ?,
   498	                event_hour_yf     = COALESCE(?, event_hour_yf),
   499	                call_datetime_utc = COALESCE(?, call_datetime_utc),
   500	                call_source       = COALESCE(?, call_source),
   501	                gcal_id           = COALESCE(?, gcal_id),
   502	                quarter           = COALESCE(?, quarter),
   503	                eps_estimate      = COALESCE(?, eps_estimate),
   504	                eps_actual        = COALESCE(?, eps_actual),
   505	                rev_estimate      = COALESCE(?, rev_estimate),
   506	                rev_actual        = COALESCE(?, rev_actual),
   507	                reported          = ?,
   508	                tier              = ?,
   509	                company_name      = COALESCE(?, company_name),
   510	                source_fingerprint = ?,
   511	                date_confirmed    = ?,
   512	                updated_at        = datetime('now')
   513	            WHERE ticker = ? AND event_date = ?
   514	            """,
   515	            (event_hour, event_hour_yf, call_datetime_utc, call_source,
   516	             gcal_id, quarter,
   517	             eps_estimate, eps_actual, rev_estimate, rev_actual,
   518	             int(reported), tier, company_name, source_fingerprint,
   519	             date_confirmed,
   520	             ticker, event_date),
   521	        )
   522	    else:
   523	        # For old DBs with UNIQUE(ticker, quarter), delete any existing row
   524	        # for this ticker+quarter before inserting with the new date.
   525	        #
   526	        # NEVER delete a row already marked reported=1. A reported event has
   527	        # already happened, so its date doesn't move — but a date-flapping
   528	        # *no-actuals* phantom from the same reporting quarter (e.g. Finnhub
   529	        # double-listing ICLR: real 2026-05-27 actuals + a phantom forward
   530	        # date) would otherwise clobber the reported row here, wiping the
   531	        # `reported` flag and causing the same actuals to re-post every run.
   532	        # Guarding on reported=0 keeps the actuals row alive. Worst case a
   533	        # genuine post-report date correction leaves a harmless duplicate
   534	        # (skipped by the actuals detector; cleaned by --cleanup), which is
   535	        # far better than losing the actuals.
   536	        if quarter:
   537	            conn.execute(
   538	                "DELETE FROM events WHERE ticker = ? AND quarter = ? "
   539	                "AND event_date != ? AND reported = 0",
   540	                (ticker, quarter, event_date),
   541	            )
   542	        conn.execute(
   543	            """
   544	            INSERT INTO events (ticker, event_date, event_hour, event_hour_yf,
   545	                                call_datetime_utc, call_source,
   546	                                gcal_id, quarter,
   547	                                eps_estimate, eps_actual, rev_estimate, rev_actual,
   548	                                reported, tier, company_name, source_fingerprint,
   549	                                date_confirmed)
   550	            VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)
   551	            """,
   552	            (ticker, event_date, event_hour, event_hour_yf,
   553	             call_datetime_utc, call_source,
   554	             gcal_id, quarter,
   555	             eps_estimate, eps_actual, rev_estimate, rev_actual,
   556	             int(reported), tier, company_name, source_fingerprint,
   557	             date_confirmed),
   558	        )
   559	
   560	    conn.commit()
   561	
   562	
   563	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   564	# Estimate history (for building revision trends)
   565	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

   329	def fetch_yfinance_earnings_datetime(ticker: str) -> list[datetime] | None:
   330	    """Backward-compat wrapper returning only release-timestamp candidates.
   331	
   332	    Kept so the existing fetch_yfinance_hour_for_date implementation and
   333	    any external callers of this name keep working without change.
   334	    Internally just unwraps the release_candidates from the new
   335	    fetch_yfinance_earnings_timestamps shape.
   336	    """
   337	    bundle = fetch_yfinance_earnings_timestamps(ticker)
   338	    if bundle is None:
   339	        return None
   340	    return bundle.release_candidates or None
   341	
   342	
   343	def infer_hour_from_datetime(dt: datetime) -> str | None:
   344	    """Classify a yfinance earnings datetime into 'bmo' / 'amc' / None
   345	    based on US market session boundaries.
   346	
   347	    Rule:
   348	      < 09:30 America/New_York  -> 'bmo'  (pre-market release)
   349	      >= 16:00 America/New_York -> 'amc'  (post-close release)
   350	      otherwise                  -> None  (mid-session, ambiguous)
   351	
   352	    The 09:30 / 16:00 boundaries are NYSE/NASDAQ regular hours. A common
   353	    pattern is press releases at 06:30 ET (BMO) or 16:05 ET (AMC); both
   354	    classify cleanly. The 8:30 ET pre-open release pattern that the
   355	    earlier <9 / >16 heuristic would have classified as None is now
   356	    correctly captured as 'bmo'.
   357	    """
   358	    if dt is None:
   359	        return None
   360	    if ZoneInfo is None:
   361	        return None
   362	    try:
   363	        et = dt.astimezone(ZoneInfo("America/New_York"))
   364	    except Exception:
   365	        return None
   366	    open_t = time(9, 30)
   367	    close_t = time(16, 0)
   368	    if et.time() < open_t:
   369	        return "bmo"
   370	    if et.time() >= close_t:

   372	    return None
   373	
   374	
   375	def fetch_yfinance_hour_for_date(ticker: str, earnings_date: str) -> str | None:
   376	    """Convenience wrapper: match a release-timestamp candidate to the
   377	    target press-release date and infer 'bmo'/'amc' from its time-of-day.
   378	
   379	    Reads release candidates only (earningsTimestamp / Start / End). Call
   380	    timestamps go through fetch_yfinance_call_for_date.
   381	
   382	    Returns None if yfinance has nothing for this ticker, no release
   383	    candidate matches the target date, or the matching candidate's time
   384	    falls inside market hours (mid-session releases are ambiguous).
   385	    """
   386	    bundle = fetch_yfinance_earnings_timestamps(ticker)
   387	    if bundle is None or not bundle.release_candidates:
   388	        return None
   389	    if ZoneInfo is None:
   390	        return None

Found High issues:

1. **High: `event_hour_yf` fallback is ignored.**  
   [consensus_preview.py](</mnt/c/Users/jroyp/Dropbox/Claude Folder/earnings_agent/consensus_preview.py:328>) selects only `event_hour`, so rows with cached yfinance timing render `TBD` and compute the wrong reaction date.  
   Repro: DB row `event_hour=NULL,event_hour_yf='bmo',event_date='2026-07-17'` -> preview uses `None`, so `reaction_date(..., None)` returns `2026-07-20` instead of `2026-07-17`.

2. **High: `dmh` implied-move reaction date is wrong.**  
   [consensus_preview.py](</mnt/c/Users/jroyp/Dropbox/Claude Folder/earnings_agent/consensus_preview.py:254>) treats only `bmo` as same-day; `dmh` falls through to next weekday, unlike the existing post-earnings move logic.  
   Repro: `reaction_date("2026-07-17", "dmh")` returns `2026-07-20`, skipping the Friday expiry for a Friday intraday report.

3. **High: Slack truncation can mark unposted rows as posted.**  
   [consensus_preview.py](</mnt/c/Users/jroyp/Dropbox/Claude Folder/earnings_agent/consensus_preview.py:1131>) truncates blocks to 48, but [main.py](</mnt/c/Users/jroyp/Dropbox/Claude Folder/earnings_agent/main.py:1713>) marks every assembled row after Slack accepts the truncated payload.  
   Repro: 24 preview rows with FMP-off `na_notes` produce 48 blocks with `T23` omitted, but `kv_set(consensus_preview_posted:T23:...)` still runs.
